Logic and Technical Terms
beginner
4 min
Definition of Place as Inner Surface
Al-Jurjani presents Aristotle's definition of place and states the alternative possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Aristotle's definition of place as the inner surface of the container and the two possibilities that arise if place is not surface.

Core Idea
Place is not a dimension but the inner surface that contains the body.

Al-Jurjani begins his discussion of place by presenting the classical definition from Aristotle, which defines place as the inner surface of the containing body. This definition is the starting point for the debate about whether place is a surface or a dimension. In this lesson, you will encounter the definition and the initial framing of the alternative view.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition and the shield example
Read the Arabic passage once, noting the example of the shield on a dome. Then read the translation to understand how place is defined as the surrounding surface.
The shield example illustrates that place is only the part that prevents descent.
2
Identify Aristotle's definition and its proponents
Notice that the author explicitly attributes the definition to Aristotle and mentions that later philosophers like Ibn Sina and al-Farabi follow it.
3
Note the conditional: if not surface, then dimension
The passage sets up the alternative: if place is not the inner surface, it must be a dimension. This prepares the ground for the refutation that follows.
This conditional is the pivot to the next lesson.

قوله : (إما أن يقبل لذاته الحركة القبول قد يطلق بمعنى الإمكان كما يقال : الماهية تقبل الوجود والعدم لذاته، وهو المراد هاهنا أي البعد إما أن يمكن له الحركة نظراً إلى ذاته، أولا يمكن له نظراً إلى ذاته ولا واسطة بين الشقين وعلى الأول يلزم التسلسل، وعلى الثاني يمنع اتصافه بالحركة. فلا يرد أنه إن أريد بعدم قبوله إياها أن يكون ذاته مقتضياً لعدم القبول، فالترديد غير حاصر لجواز أن لا يكون متقضياً للقبول ولا لعدمه وإن أريد به عدم اتصافه بالقبول نظراً إلى ذاته فلا نسلم لزوم امتناع قبول الجسم للحركة لجواز أن يكون البعد قابلاً لها بتبع الجسم، وإن لم يكن قابلاً لها بذاته .

النزول وهو ممتنع فإنا نشاهد كلاً منها متحركاً والحركة، لا بد أن يكون عن شيء إلى شيء وما منه الانتقال وإليه، هو المكان كذا في الأبكار.

قوله : ( ألا ترى إلخ) وذلك لأن المراد بخروج كل واحد خروج كل بعد سواء كان مجتمعاً مع آخر أولا فإذا خرج كل واحد بهذا المعنى خرج الكل وليس المراد خروج كل واحد بشرط الانفراد عن الآخر حتى لا يستلزم الحكم على كل واحد الحكم على الكل، كما في قولنا كل رجل يشبعه هذا الرغيف .
The second observation - the ninth objective: Place, and it is of continuous quantity. The surrounding [surface] until if a shield is placed on the head of a dome to the extent of a dirham, they only considered its place to be the amount that prevents it from descending. The first possibility: that it (i.e., place) is the inner surface of the container tangent to the outer surface of the contained, and this is the doctrine of Aristotle. The later philosophers such as Ibn Sina and al-Farabi and their followers are upon it. Otherwise, i.e., if place were not the surface, it would be dimension, as it has passed that it does not exit from them. And that it, i.e., its being a dimension, is impossible. As for the supposed dimension, it has passed that it exists by the four aspects indicating that. And as for the existing dimension, it is [refuted] by two arguments. The first: that that dimension either accepts motion in space (al-haraka al-ayniyya) by its essence or does not accept it. Both divisions are false. As for the first, because if the dimension accepted spatial motion, then from place to place, for there is no meaning of spatial motion except transition. Then after that it has another place and it leads to an infinite regress, and there would be infinite dimensions interpenetrating each other. And that is necessarily impossible. And how could it not be impossible? And all those places, inasmuch as they are all, all of them can be transferred. Because if the transfer of each one is possible, then the transfer of the whole inasmuch as it is a whole is also possible. Do you not see that if each one leaves its place, then the whole has left. So it, i.e., the whole, has a place. That place is inside those places because it is one of them, and outside them because it is a container for them. This is a contradiction because it combines two opposites. His saying: 'Either it accepts motion by its essence' – acceptance may be used in the sense of possibility, as it is said: essence accepts existence and non-existence by its essence, and that is intended here. That is, the dimension either can have motion with respect to its essence, or cannot have it with respect to its essence, and there is no middle ground between the two. On the first, an infinite regress follows; on the second, it prevents it from being described by motion. So it is not objected that if by its not accepting it is meant that its essence necessitates non-acceptance, then the dichotomy is not exhaustive for it is possible that it does not necessitate acceptance nor its opposite. And if what is intended is that it is not described with acceptance with respect to its essence, then we do not grant the necessity of the impossibility of the body's acceptance of motion, because it is possible that the dimension is capable of it by following the body, even if it is not capable of it by its essence. His saying: 'Because if it accepted motion etc.' – its summary is that if motion were possible for it, then place would be possible for it, and if place were possible for it, then the impossible would be possible, which is the existence of infinite dimensions. Or it is said: if it were possible, then from the assumption of its occurrence an impossibility would not follow with respect to its essence, but the impossibility follows, so it repels what is imagined that acceptance of motion does not necessitate the actual occurrence of motions such that it would have another place, rather the possibility of place [is sufficient], and that does not necessitate an infinite regress. The descent, and it is impossible, for we witness each of them moving, and motion must be from something to something, and what the transition is from and to is place, as in al-Abkar. His saying: 'Even if a shield is placed' – a shield (darqa) is a shield made of leather without wood or sinew. His saying: 'By the four aspects indicating that' – he only attributed indication to them because they are reminders of the existence of place. Otherwise, it has preceded that what is beneficial for that is rational necessity. His saying: 'As for the first, because if the dimension accepted motion etc.' – it is answered by choosing the first branch and denying the necessity of infinite regress, because acceptance of motion is an expression of the possibility of being described by transition from place to place, and this possibility necessitates the possibility that the described has a place, not its necessity, so infinite regress does not follow. But there is consideration in this; because the necessity of infinite regress and the realization of infinite dimensions is not due to the description of each dimension with spatial motion actually, such that what was mentioned would be refuted, but rather because that which is capable of spatial motion must be something actually occupying place. For what is not related to place, like abstract entities, is not capable of it at all, and the opponent also acknowledges this. And the commentator will explicitly state in… His saying: 'Do you not see etc.' – that is because what is meant by each one leaving is the leaving of each dimension, whether it is combined with another or not. So if each one leaves in this sense, the whole leaves. What is not intended is each one leaving under the condition of being separate from the other, such that the judgment on each one does not entail the judgment on the whole, as in our statement: every man, this loaf satisfies him.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage presents the definition of place as the inner surface of the container (Aristotle's view) and begins refuting the alternative view that place is a dimension. The author first states the two possibilities: if place is not surface, it must be dimension. Then he argues that the dimension view is impossible. The proof is divided: for the supposed dimension (already proved impossible by four aspects) and for the existing dimension, which is refuted by two arguments. The passage covers the first argument in detail: either dimension accepts spatial motion or not. Both are false. If it accepts motion, it would need another place, leading to an infinite regress of interpenetrating dimensions, which is impossible. The author then explains the absurdity further: if all those places can be transferred, the whole has a place that is both inside and outside them—a contradiction. The marginal comments clarify the terminology: 'acceptance' means possibility, and the dichotomy is exhaustive. They also address an objection: possibility of motion does not necessitate actual motion, but the commentator argues that the capacity for motion requires actual occupancy of place, leading to infinite regress. The comment on 'Do you not see' explains that the whole's leaving follows from each part leaving, not under the condition of separateness.

Checkpoint
According to Aristotle, place is:
A) The volume occupied by the body
B) The inner surface of the container
C) The outer surface of the body
D) The dimension between two bodies

Key Takeaway
Aristotle defines place as the inner surface of the containing body.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that, according to Aristotle, your place is not the space you fill but the surface that holds you. What 'inner surface' in your life—a habit, a relationship, a comfort zone—defines your boundaries? Are you letting that surface be your place, or are you reaching beyond it to the One who is not contained by any surface?
?
The shield on the dome is kept from falling by only a small contact point. Reflect: What small 'contact point' of faith prevents your soul from descending into despair? Is it just one verse, one du'a, one moment of sincerity? How can you strengthen that point today?
